                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">سَمَعَ</orth>
                  </form>, (K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">سَمْعٌ</foreign> (S Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">سِمْعٌ</foreign>, or this latter is a simple subst., (Lh, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">سَمَاعٌ</foreign>, (S, K,) or this last [also] is a simple subst., (Msb,) and <foreign lang="ar">سَمَاعَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">سَمَاعِيَةٌ</foreign> (K) and <foreign lang="ar">مَسْمَعٌ</foreign>, (TA,) [<hi rend="ital">He heard it,</hi> (namely, a thing, as in the S,) or <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">him;</hi>] and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20710-1" target="تسمّع" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20710"/></foreign>, (Msb, K,) also written and pronounced <foreign lang="ar">اِسَّمَّعَ</foreign>; (K, TA;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20710-2" target="استمع" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (Msb;) are syn. with <foreign lang="ar">سَمِعَ</foreign> (Msb,K) as trans. By itself; (Msb;) and <foreign lang="ar">استمع</foreign> [also] in sys. With <foreign lang="ar">سَمِعَ</foreign> [ as trans. by itself]: (Ham p. 694, where occurs a usage of its act. part. n. showing the verb to be trans. by itself:) or   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20710-3" target="استمع" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> denotes what is intentional, signifying only <hi rend="ital">he gave ear, hearkened,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">listened:</hi> but <foreign lang="ar">سَمِعَ</foreign>, [as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20710-4" target="تمسمّع" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20710"/></foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20710-5" target="استسمع" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>,] what is unintentional, as well as what is intentional. (Msb.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">سَمِعَ الشَّىْءَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He heard</hi> or <hi rend="ital">listened to, the thing</hi>] (S.) And <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20710-6" target="تسمّع" n="6" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n20710"/>الصَّوْتَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He listened to,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">heard, the sound</hi>]. (TA.) [And <foreign lang="ar">سَمِعْتُ لَهُ صَوْتًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I heard him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, utter,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">produce, a sound;</hi> lit. <hi rend="ital">I heard a sound attributable to him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it.</hi> And <foreign lang="ar">سَمِعَهُ مِنْهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He heard it form him.</hi> And <foreign lang="ar">سَمِعَهُ عَنْهُ</foreign>

                  <hi rend="ital">He heard him say such a thing.</hi>] And <foreign lang="ar">سَمِعَ بِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He heard of it;</hi> for <foreign lang="ar">سَمِعَ التَّكَلُّمَ بِهِ</foreign>, or the like]. (Kur xii. 31 and xxviii. 36 and xxxviii. 6, S, K, TA.) [When trans. by means of <foreign lang="ar">لِ</foreign> alone, or <foreign lang="ar">إِلَى</foreign>, it denotes what is intentional.] You say, <foreign lang="ar">سَمِعْتُ لَهُ</foreign>, (S, Msb, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">إِلَيْهِ</foreign>, (S, TA,) meaning <hi rend="ital">I gave ear, hearkened,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">listened, to him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it;</hi> (S, Msb, * TA;) and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20710-7" target="تسمّعت" n="7" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n20710"/>له</foreign> (Msb,) or <foreign lang="ar">اليه</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">اِسَّمَّعْتُ</foreign>, (S, TA,) signify the same; (S, Msb, TA;) and so <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20710-8" target="استمعت" n="8" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>له</foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">اليه</foreign>. (K.) It is said in the Kur [xxxvii. 8], accord. to different readings, <foreign lang="ar">لَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يَسْمَعُونَ إِلَى المَلَإِ الأَعْلَى</foreign>, and   
      <foreign lang="ar">لَا <ref cref="n20710-9" target="يَسَّمَّعُونَ" n="9" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, <hi rend="ital">They shall not listen</hi> [<hi rend="ital">to the archangels</hi>]: (S:) or the former has this signification, <hi rend="ital">they shall not listen to the angels</hi> (Bd, Jel) <hi rend="ital">in heaven,</hi> (Jel,) or <hi rend="ital">the exalted angels:</hi> (Bd:) and ↓ the latter, <hi rend="ital">they shall not seek,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">endeavour, to listen</hi> &amp;c. (Bd.) And in the same [xvii. 50],   
      <foreign lang="ar">نَحْنُ أَعْلَمُ بِمَا <ref cref="n20710-10" target="يَسْتَمِعُونَ" n="10" lang="ar" type="7" subtype="WOTF"/> بِهِ إِذْ يَسْتَمِعُونَ إِلَيْكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">We are cognizant of that on account of which they hearken when they hearken to thee</hi>]; <foreign lang="ar">به</foreign> meaning <foreign lang="ar">بِسَبَبِهِ</foreign>, (Bd, Jel,) and <foreign lang="ar">لِأَجْلِهِ</foreign>, (Bd,) alluding to scoffing, or derision. (Bd, Jel.) [For various usages of <foreign lang="ar">سَمْعٌ</foreign> and other inf. ns., whether employed as inf. ns. or as simple substs., see those words below.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  It also signifies <hi rend="ital">He understood it;</hi> (TA;) <hi rend="ital">he understood its meaning;</hi> i. e., the meaning of a person's speech. (Msb.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">لَمْ تَسْمَعْ مَا قُلْتُ لَكَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Thou didst not understand what I said to thee.</hi> (TA.) And such is the most obvious meaning of the verb in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">إِنْ كَانَ يَسْمَعُ الخَطِيبَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">If he understand the words of the preacher</hi>]; for this is the proper meaning in this case: but it may be rendered tropically, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">if he hear the voice of the preacher.</hi> (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">He knew it:</hi> as in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">سَمِعَ ٱللّٰهُ قَوْلَكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">God knew thy saying</hi>]. (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  Also <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He accepted it;</hi> namely, evidence, and praise: or, said of the latter, <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">he recompensed it by acceptance:</hi> (Msb:) <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">he paid regard to it, and answered it;</hi> namely, prayer: <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">he answered,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">assented to,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">complied with, it;</hi> namely, a person's speech. (TA.) The saying <foreign lang="ar">سَمِعَ ٱللّٰهُ لِمَنْ حَمِدَهُ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">May God accept the praise of him who praiseth Him:</hi> or, accord. to IAmb, <hi rend="ital">may God recompense by acceptance the praise of him who praiseth Him:</hi> (Msb:) or <hi rend="ital">may God answer the prayer of him who praiseth Him.</hi> (TA, as on the authority of IAmb.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  Also <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He obeyed him:</hi> as in the saying in the Kur [xxxvi. 24], <foreign lang="ar">إِنِّى آمَنْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ فَٱسْمَعُونِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">Verily I believe in your Lord, and do ye obey me</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  Lth says that the phrase <foreign lang="ar">سَمِعَتْ أُذُنِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">زَيْدًا يَفْعَلُ كَذَا وَكَذَا</foreign> means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">My eye saw Zeyd doing such and such things:</hi> but Az says, I know not whence Lth brought this; for it is not of the way of the Arabs to say <foreign lang="ar">سمعت اذنى</foreign> as meaning <hi rend="ital">my eye saw:</hi> it is in my judgment corrupt language, and I am not sure but that it may have been originated by those addicted to innovations and erroneous opinions.                   <hi rend="ital">tive</hi>]; both signifying the same. (TA.) [And <foreign lang="ar">سمّع بِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He made to hear of it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">him.</hi>] It is said in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ سَمَّعَ النَّاسَ بِعَمَلِهِ سَمَّعَ ٱللّٰهُ بِهِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَسَامِعَ خَلْقِهِ وَحَقَّرَهُ وَصَغَّرَهُ</foreign> (S, * Mgh, TA) [<hi rend="ital">Whoso maketh men to hear of his deed,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">God will make the ears of his creatures to hear of him</hi> on the day of resurrection; (TA;) or <hi rend="ital">whoso maketh his deed notorious, that men may see it and hear of it, God will make notorious his hypocrisy, and fill with it the ears of his creatures, and they shall be generally acquainted with it,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">and He will render him contemptible, and small in estimation,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">so that he will become disgraced;</hi> (Mgh;) or the meaning may be, <hi rend="ital">God will manifest to men his internal state, and fill their ears with the evilness of his secret intentions,</hi> in requital of his deed: or, as some relate it, [for <foreign lang="ar">أَسَامِعَ خَلْقِهِ</foreign>] we should say, <foreign lang="ar">سَامِعُ خَلْقِهِ</foreign>, which is an epithet applied to God; so that the meaning is, <hi rend="ital">Go</hi> [<hi rend="ital">the Hearer of his creatures</hi>] <hi rend="ital">will disgrace him:</hi> (TA:) [for]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">سمّع به</foreign>, (S, Mgh, Msb,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَسْمِيعٌ</foreign>, (S, Mgh, K,) signifies [also] <hi rend="ital">He rendered him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, notorious,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">infamous:</hi> (S, Mgh, K: *) or <hi rend="ital">he spread it abroad, for men to speak of it.</hi> (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">He raised him from obscurity to fame.</hi> (S, K. *)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And <hi rend="ital">He made him to hear what was bad, evil, abominable,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">foul,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">he reviled him:</hi> (AZ, T and L in art. <foreign lang="ar">ند</foreign>:) and

      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20715-1" target="سَمَاعٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20725"/></foreign>, (S, K,) [&amp;c.,] or the latter is a simple subst. [used in the abstract sense of the former]. (Msb.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">سَمْعًا وَطَاعَةً</foreign>, [for <foreign lang="ar">أَسْمَعُ سَمْعًا وَأُطِيعُ طَاعَةً</foreign>, an emphatic mode of expression, meaning <hi rend="ital">I hear and I obey,</hi> or for <foreign lang="ar">سَمِعْتُ سَمْعًا وَأَطَعْتُ طَاعَةً</foreign>, which means the same, but more emphatically; <foreign lang="ar">طَاعَةً</foreign> being a quasi-inf. n. for <foreign lang="ar">إِطَاعَةً</foreign>;] the verb [of each] being understood: and <foreign lang="ar">سَمْعٌ وَطَاعَةٌ</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">أَمْرِى ذٰلِكَ</foreign> [i. e. <foreign lang="ar">أَمْرِى سَمْعٌ وَطَاعَةٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">My affair is hearing and obeying</hi>]. (K.) You say also, [in like manner,] <foreign lang="ar">اَللّٰهُمَّ سَمْعًا لَا بَلْغًا</foreign>, (K,) and <foreign lang="ar">سَمْعٌ لَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَلْغٌ</foreign>: (TA:) see <foreign lang="ar">سِمْعٌ</foreign>. And <foreign lang="ar">سَمْعُ أُذُنِى فُلَانًا يَقُولَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ذٰلِكَ</foreign>, (K,) [said to be] the only instance of the kind among inf. ns. of trans. verbs except <foreign lang="ar">رَأْىُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَيْنِى</foreign>, (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">رأى</foreign>,) [in a copy of the M, in art. <foreign lang="ar">رأى</foreign>, written <foreign lang="ar">سَمْعَ اذنى</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">رَأْىَ عينى</foreign>,] and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20715-2" target="سِمْعُ" n="2" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>اذنى</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20715-3" target="سَمْعَةُ" n="3" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>اذنى</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20715-4" target="سِمْعَةُ" n="4" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>اذنى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">My ear heard</hi> (lit. <hi rend="ital">my ear's hearing</hi>) <hi rend="ital">such a one say that</hi>]. (K)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [As a simple subst., it signifies] The <hi rend="ital">sense of the ear;</hi> (K;) [i. e., <hi rend="ital">of hearing;</hi>] the <hi rend="ital">faculty in the ear whereby it perceives sounds.</hi> (TA.) Thus in the Kur [1. 36], <foreign lang="ar">أَوْ أَلْقَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">السَّمْعُ</foreign>, (TA,) meaning, <hi rend="ital">Or who hearkeneth.</hi> (Bd, Jel.) [And hence,] <foreign lang="ar">أُمُّ السَّمْعِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The brain;</hi> (Z, O, K;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar">أُمُّ <ref cref="n20715-5" target="السَّمِيعِ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>. (O, K.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَهُ عَلَى أُمِّ السَّمْعِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He struck him upon the brain</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [It is also used for the inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">أَسْمَعَ</foreign>. (Sb, K.) And   
      <foreign lang="ar">كَلَّمَهُ <ref cref="n20715-9" target="سِمْعَهُمْ" n="9" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, with kesr, meaning, [<hi rend="ital">He spoke to him making them to hear,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">so that they heard.</hi> (TA.) And a poet says, <quote>

                  <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سَمْعٌ</foreign>, either as an inf. n. or as a a simple subst. (Lh, K.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">اَللّٰهُمَّ سِمْعًا لَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِلْغًا</foreign>, (S, K,) and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20716-1" target="سَمْعًا" n="1" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>لَا بَلْغًا</foreign>, (K,) and <foreign lang="ar">سِمْعٌ لَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِلْغٌ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20716-2" target="سَمْعٌ" n="2" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n20715"/>لَا بَلْغٌ</foreign>, (TA,) a form of prayer, (K,) meaning <hi rend="ital">O God, may it be heard of but not fulfilled:</hi> (S, K:) or <hi rend="ital">may it be heard but not come to:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">may it be heard but not need to be come to:</hi> or it is said by him who hears tidings not pleasing to him: (K:) Ks says that it means <hi rend="ital">I hear of calamities but may they not come to me.</hi> (TA.) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">سِمْعُ أُذُنِى فُلَانًا يَقُولُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ذٰلِكَ</foreign>: see <foreign lang="ar">سَمْعٌ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">إِسْمَاعٌ</foreign>: so in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">قَالُوا ذٰلِكَ سِمْعَ أُذُنِى</foreign>: (K:) and in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">كَلَّمَهُ سِمْعَهُمْ</foreign>: (TA:) both explained above: see <foreign lang="ar">سَمْعٌ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">Mention, fame, report, that is heard;</hi> as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20716-3" target="سَمْعٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20715"/></foreign>, and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20716-4" target="سَمَاعٌ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20725"/></foreign>: (K:) <hi rend="ital">fame,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">good report;</hi> (S, Msb, K, TA;) and so   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20716-5" target="سَمْعٌ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20715"/></foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20716-6" target="سَمَاعٌ" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20725"/></foreign>. (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">ذَهَبَ سِمْعُهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فِى النَّاسِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">His fame,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">good report, went among mankind.</hi> (S.) And the Arabs say, <foreign lang="ar">لَا <ref cref="n20716-7" target="وَسَمْعِ" n="7" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> [or <foreign lang="ar">وَسِمْعِ اللّٰه</foreign>,] meaning <foreign lang="ar">لَا وَ ذِكْرِ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">No, by the glory of God</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [It is also used as an <pb n="1429"/> epithet: thus,] <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلٌ سِمْعٌ</foreign> means <foreign lang="ar">يُسَمِّعُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">A man who makes</hi> others <hi rend="ital">to hear</hi> of him]: or one says, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا ٱمْرُؤٌ ذُو سِمْعٍ</foreign>, and
